What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
The Origin of Ilm al-Kalam: Ancient or New?
Poses the question of origin and presents two contrasting views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major views on the origin of ilm al-kalam and the debate surrounding its historical roots.

Core Idea
The origin of ilm al-kalam is debated: Greek vs. Islamic beginnings.

Many people wonder whether ilm al-kalam is an ancient science passed down from earlier civilizations or a new science created by Muslims. This lesson explores the two contrasting opinions presented in the source, setting the stage for understanding the science's purpose.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the origin debate
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the question and the differing views.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Notice that some scholars claim Greek origin, while others claim Islamic origin as a defensive tool.
3
Reflect on the significance of the debate
Consider why the origin matters for understanding the nature of ilm al-kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علم الكلام بين القبول والرفض

يتساءل كثير من غير المشتغلين بالدراسات والأبحاث الفلسفية والعقدية عن ماهية علم الكلام أهو علم قديم موغل في القدم، عرفته البشرية في تاريخها الطويل من يوم أن كان لها علم ومعرفة وعلمه السابق للاحق، حتى وصل إلينا . . ؟ أم إنه علم جديد مبتكر أنشأته الأمة الإسلامية، في فترة من فترات تاريخها . . ؟ الحقيقة أن أقوال الراصدين لهذا العلم والمشتغلين بقواعده ومبادئه يتباينون ويختلفون، فالبعض منهم يرى أنه علم نشأ في دولة اليونان قديماً، ووفد إلى بلادنا فيما وفد إلينا من أفكار وآراء وفلسفات. بينما يرى البعض الآخر أنه علم جديد نشأ في دولة الإسلام، لتدافع بأسلحته الكلامية تلبيس المبطلين وغارات المغيرين، وحقد الحاقدين على عقائدها الإيمانية . واعتقد أن وقوف الباحث على أي من تعريفات هذا العلم تقرب له تاريخ نشأته، وأسباب قيامه . ولقد وضع العلماء الكلام لعلمهم هذا تعريفات كثيرة، تتباين بمقدار اقتراب صاحبها من الفلسفة أو بعده عنها .
Ilm al-kalam between acceptance and rejection. Many of those not engaged in philosophical and doctrinal studies and researches ask about the nature of ilm al-kalam: Is it an ancient science, deeply rooted in antiquity, known to humanity in its long history from the day it had knowledge and acquaintance, transmitted from the predecessor to the successor until it reached us...? Or is it a new, innovative science that the Islamic ummah created in one period of its history...? The truth is that the statements of those observing this science and those engaged in its rules and principles vary and differ. Some of them see that it is a science that originated in the land of the Greeks long ago, and came to our lands among the ideas, opinions, and philosophies that came to us. While others see that it is a new science that originated in the land of Islam, in order to defend with its kalam weapons the obfuscation of the falsehood-practitioners, the raids of the attackers, and the hatred of the haters against its theological doctrines. And I believe that the researcher's acquaintance with any of the definitions of this science brings near to him the history of its origin and the reasons for its establishment. And the kalam scholars have laid down for their science many definitions, differing according to the degree of the definer's closeness to philosophy or distance from it.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage opens with a heading 'Ilm al-kalam between acceptance and rejection,' then poses a fundamental question about the nature of this science: is it an ancient science inherited from earlier civilizations, or a new science created by the Islamic ummah? The author notes that observers disagree: some claim Greek origin, others claim an Islamic origin as a defensive tool. The author then offers his own view that studying the definitions of kalam can reveal its history and reasons for emergence. Finally, he notes that scholars have produced many definitions, which vary according to how close the definer is to philosophy. This passage sets up a historiographical debate and emphasizes the interpretative role of definitions in understanding the science.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
العقائد الإيمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all scholars agree ilm al-kalam has a single origin.
Correction: The author shows that there are two distinct views, with no consensus.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the proposed origins of ilm al-kalam?
A) Greek
B) Persian
C) Indian
D) Egyptian

Key Takeaway
Ilm al-kalam's origin is disputed between a Greek origin and an Islamic origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before reading this lesson, did you have a default assumption about where ilm al-kalam came from? Are you willing to hold that assumption lightly, acknowledging that even scholars disagree? What would it cost you to remain uncertain about this?
?
This passage does not tell you which view is correct—it simply presents the debate. Are you comfortable with ambiguity in religious knowledge, or do you feel a need to settle things quickly? Ask yourself: Do I trust that Allah's guidance is enough even when historical details are unclear?
?
The second view says ilm al-kalam arose to defend against 'the obfuscation of falsehood-practitioners.' Think of a time you felt your faith was challenged by an idea. Did you have the tools to respond? If not, what would it take to learn them—and what is stopping you?

Definitions as Clues to Ilm al-Kalam's Origin
Discusses the role of definitions in revealing the history and causes of ilm al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the definitions of ilm al-kalam can reveal its history and how they vary based on philosophical influence.

Core Idea
Definitions of ilm al-kalam reflect its history and proximity to philosophy.

The author suggests that by examining the definitions of ilm al-kalam, we can gain insight into its origin and purpose. This lesson focuses on the final part of the passage, where the author explains that definitions vary according to the definer's closeness to philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definitions
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the author's claim about definitions.
2
Identify the key claim
Note that the author believes definitions bring near the history and reasons for the science's emergence.
3
Analyze the variation in definitions
Understand that definitions differ based on how close the definer is to philosophy.

Source Text

علم الكلام بين القبول والرفض

يتساءل كثير من غير المشتغلين بالدراسات والأبحاث الفلسفية والعقدية عن ماهية علم الكلام أهو علم قديم موغل في القدم، عرفته البشرية في تاريخها الطويل من يوم أن كان لها علم ومعرفة وعلمه السابق للاحق، حتى وصل إلينا . . ؟ أم إنه علم جديد مبتكر أنشأته الأمة الإسلامية، في فترة من فترات تاريخها . . ؟ الحقيقة أن أقوال الراصدين لهذا العلم والمشتغلين بقواعده ومبادئه يتباينون ويختلفون، فالبعض منهم يرى أنه علم نشأ في دولة اليونان قديماً، ووفد إلى بلادنا فيما وفد إلينا من أفكار وآراء وفلسفات. بينما يرى البعض الآخر أنه علم جديد نشأ في دولة الإسلام، لتدافع بأسلحته الكلامية تلبيس المبطلين وغارات المغيرين، وحقد الحاقدين على عقائدها الإيمانية . واعتقد أن وقوف الباحث على أي من تعريفات هذا العلم تقرب له تاريخ نشأته، وأسباب قيامه . ولقد وضع العلماء الكلام لعلمهم هذا تعريفات كثيرة، تتباين بمقدار اقتراب صاحبها من الفلسفة أو بعده عنها .
Ilm al-kalam between acceptance and rejection. Many of those not engaged in philosophical and doctrinal studies and researches ask about the nature of ilm al-kalam: Is it an ancient science, deeply rooted in antiquity, known to humanity in its long history from the day it had knowledge and acquaintance, transmitted from the predecessor to the successor until it reached us...? Or is it a new, innovative science that the Islamic ummah created in one period of its history...? The truth is that the statements of those observing this science and those engaged in its rules and principles vary and differ. Some of them see that it is a science that originated in the land of the Greeks long ago, and came to our lands among the ideas, opinions, and philosophies that came to us. While others see that it is a new science that originated in the land of Islam, in order to defend with its kalam weapons the obfuscation of the falsehood-practitioners, the raids of the attackers, and the hatred of the haters against its theological doctrines. And I believe that the researcher's acquaintance with any of the definitions of this science brings near to him the history of its origin and the reasons for its establishment. And the kalam scholars have laid down for their science many definitions, differing according to the degree of the definer's closeness to philosophy or distance from it.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage opens with a heading 'Ilm al-kalam between acceptance and rejection,' then poses a fundamental question about the nature of this science: is it an ancient science inherited from earlier civilizations, or a new science created by the Islamic ummah? The author notes that observers disagree: some claim Greek origin, others claim an Islamic origin as a defensive tool. The author then offers his own view that studying the definitions of kalam can reveal its history and reasons for emergence. Finally, he notes that scholars have produced many definitions, which vary according to how close the definer is to philosophy. This passage sets up a historiographical debate and emphasizes the interpretative role of definitions in understanding the science.

Key Terms
تعريفات
الفلسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That definitions of ilm al-kalam are uniform and objective.
Correction: The author points out that definitions vary significantly based on the definer's philosophical stance.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what can help one understand the history and origin of ilm al-kalam?
A) The opinions of philosophers
B) The definitions of the science
C) The political history of Islam
D) The attacks of haters

Key Takeaway
The definitions of ilm al-kalam are key to understanding its history and vary with philosophical influence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a definition of an Islamic term, do you ask yourself what background or bias the definer might have? How might this lesson change the way you receive such definitions?
?
The author claims definitions reveal the history and causes of a science. What does your own understanding of Islamic theology reveal about the history and influences that shaped it? Are you willing to examine that honestly?

What Is Kalam?

The Origin of Kalam: Ancient or New?
Author poses the question of kalam's origin and presents two opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scholarly views on the historical origin of ilm al-kalam and why the question matters.

Core Idea
The origin of kalam is debated: was it ancient Greek or Islamic-born?

This passage opens the study of ilm al-kalam by addressing a fundamental question: where did this science come from? Before diving into definitions and arguments, the author wants us to situate kalam historically. He presents two opposing camps: one traces it to Greece, the other to early Islam. By reading, we set the stage for deeper investigation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage through without annotation. Then read the translation. Let the author's own framing come through.
Notice the rhetorical question at the beginning.
2
Identify the two views
The passage presents two opposing views on kalam's origin. Find the sentences that describe each view and note how they differ.
3
Examine the author's suggestion
The author says that studying definitions of kalam will reveal its history. Reflect on why definitions might be the key to understanding origins.
This connects definitions to historical context.
4
Reflect on the debate's significance
Think about why the origin of a science matters. How might the answer affect how we study kalam today?
This prepares you for the definitions that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علم الكلام بين القبول والرفض
يتساءل كثير من غير المشتغلين بالدراسات والأبحاث الفلسفية والعقدية عن ماهية علم الكلام أهو علم قديم موغل في القدم، عرفته البشرية في تاريخها الطويل من يوم أن كان لها علم ومعرفة وعلمه السابق للاحق، حتى وصل إلينا . . ؟
أم إنه علم جديد مبتكر أنشأته الأمة الإسلامية، في فترة من فترات
تاريخها . . ؟
الحقيقة أن أقوال الراصدين لهذا العلم والمشتغلين بقواعده ومبادئه يتباينون ويختلفون، فالبعض منهم يرى أنه علم نشأ في دولة اليونان قديماً، ووفد إلى بلادنا فيما وفد إلينا من أفكار وآراء وفلسفات.
بينما يرى البعض الآخر أنه علم جديد نشأ في دولة الإسلام، لتدافع بأسلحته الكلامية تلبيس المبطلين وغارات المغيرين، وحقد الحاقدين على عقائدها الإيمانية .
واعتقد أن وقوف الباحث على أي من تعريفات هذا العلم تقرب له تاريخ
نشأته، وأسباب قيامه .
ولقد وضع العلماء الكلام لعلمهم هذا تعريفات كثيرة، تتباين بمقدار اقتراب صاحبها من الفلسفة أو بعده عنها .
The Kalam between acceptance and rejection. Many non-specialists in philosophical and doctrinal studies and research ask about the essence of ilm al-kalam: is it an ancient science, deep in antiquity, known to humanity in its long history from the day it had science and knowledge, with its earlier part taught to the later, until it reached us...? Or is it a new, innovative science that the Islamic nation established in a period of its history...? The truth is that the statements of those who observe this science and those engaged in its rules and principles vary and differ. Some of them see it as a science that originated in ancient Greece and came to our lands among the ideas, opinions, and philosophies that came to us. While others see it as a new science that originated in the Islamic state, to defend with its verbal weapons the falsehoods of the falsifiers, the attacks of the attackers, and the hatred of the haters against its creedal beliefs. And I believe that the researcher's acquaintance with any of the definitions of this science approximates for him the history of its origin and the reasons for its establishment. And indeed, the scholars of kalam have set for this science of theirs many definitions, varying according to the extent of their author's proximity to or distance from philosophy.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is an introductory section that raises the question of the historical origin of ilm al-kalam. The author begins by noting that many people wonder if kalam is an ancient science, known since the dawn of human knowledge, or a new science invented by the Islamic community. He then presents two opposing scholarly views: one holds that kalam originated in ancient Greece and was transmitted to the Islamic world along with other philosophical ideas; the other holds that it is a new science created within Islam to defend its doctrines from internal and external attacks. The author suggests that examining the definitions of kalam will give insight into its history. He concludes by remarking that scholars have given many definitions, which vary according to how close or far their authors are from philosophy. This passage sets the stage for the subsequent presentation of a specific definition by Ibn Khaldun.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
اليونان
الفلسفة
العقائد الإيمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the two opposing views on the origin of ilm al-kalam?
A) It originated in ancient Greece.
B) It originated in the Byzantine Empire.
C) It originated in Persia.
D) It is of unknown origin.

Key Takeaway
Ilm al-kalam has disputed origins—some trace it to Greece, others see it as an Islamic innovation to defend creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before reading this lesson, did you assume that Islamic sciences like kalam have purely Islamic origins? How does the existence of a Greek origin theory challenge the way you approach the history of your own beliefs? Will you now investigate the roots of other Islamic sciences?
?
The author says that definitions of kalam reveal its origin and purpose. What 'definitions' or labels have you accepted about your own faith without questioning their origin? Are you willing to examine them now?
?
The passage presents two conflicting views without immediately settling the debate. How comfortable are you with uncertainty in matters of religious knowledge? What does this teach you about the process of seeking truth?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
6 min
Ibn Khaldun's Definition of Kalam and Its Scope
Author presents Ibn Khaldun's definition and raises the scope question.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Khaldun's definition of ilm al-kalam and the critical question it raises about whether the discipline is limited to defending Sunni creed or encompasses all theological positions.

Core Idea
Ibn Khaldun defines kalam as rational defense of Sunni creed against innovators.

What exactly is ilm al-kalam? Modern readers might think of abstract theology, but Ibn Khaldun's definition grounds it in a defensive mission. His definition, chosen here because it predates later philosophical influences, highlights that kalam is fundamentally about protecting creedal beliefs using reason. This lesson unpacks that definition and the provocative question it inspires about the scope of the field.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read Ibn Khaldun's definition of kalam carefully. Notice what he includes and excludes. What is the purpose of the science according to him?
Pay attention to the phrase 'defending creedal beliefs' – this sets the tone.
2
Analyze the three features
After presenting the definition, the author extracts three key features: kalam defends creed, uses rational proofs, and targets innovators. Reflect on how each feature shapes the identity of kalam.
These features are not explicitly numbered but are clearly distinct.
3
Consider the scope question
The author then asks: if kalam is defined as defending Sunni creed, what about similar sciences used by other sects? Read the question carefully and think about its implications for the definition itself.
The question challenges whether kalam is a 'sectarian' science or a universal method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أردنا أن نقدم بين يدي القارىء أحد هذه التعريفات، فإننا نختار التعريف الذي قدمه ابن خلدون في مقدمته باعتباره يمثل المرحلة الأولى من نشأة هذا العلم، قبل اختلاطه بالفلسفة، وهو مع ذلك يكاد يعبر عن رأي الأغلبية ممن يشتغلون بهذا العلم .
يقول ابن خلدون : وهو علم يتضمن الحجاج عن العقائد الإيمانة بالأدلة العقلية، والرد على المبتدعة المنحرفين في الاعتقادات عن مذهب السلف، أو أهل السنة» (١) .
والتعريف الذي قدمه ابن خلدون يعطينا عند فحصه وتأمله أن علم الكلام
علم يدافع عن العقائد الإيمانية (٢) .
وأسلحته الدفاعية هي العقل ومعداته .
وهو دائماً يشهر في وجه المبتدعة الضالين .
وإذا كان ذلك كذلك. فبماذا يسمى الآخر الذي يستعمله خصوم أهل السنة والجماعة من الجهمية والخوارج والباطنية، وبقية الفرق الضالة الخارجة عن مذهب السلف؟ .
إن صاحب كتاب (كشاف اصطلاحات الفنون يتساءل أيضاً فيقول: «هل علم الكلام يشمل الدفاع عن عقيدة أهل السنة والجماعة فقط؟ أو يشمل كل العقائد المتعلقة بأصول الدين؟ سواء منها الموافق، أو المخالف؟ وإذا كان
(۱) راجع مقدمة ابن خلدون ص ٤٤٨ ط المكتبة التجارية الكبرى - مصر . وقال الفارابي : «إن الكلام صناعة يقتدر بها الإنسان على نصرة الآراء والأفعال المحدودة التي صرح بها واضع الملة، وتزييف كل ما خالف من الأقاويل إحصاء العلوم ص ۷۱ - ۷۲ . (۲) قال الإمام الغزالي : لما نشأت صيغة الكلام وكثر الخوض فيه تشوق المتكلمون إلى محاولة الذب عن السنة بالبحث عن حقائق الأمور، وخاضوا في البحث عن الجواهر والأعراض، وأحكامهما،
ولكن لما لم يكن ذلك مقصودهم، لم يبلغ كلامهم فيه الغاية القصوى.
(راجع المنقذ من الضلال فصل علم الكلام .
٢٤
And if we want to present to the reader one of these definitions, we choose the definition given by Ibn Khaldun in his Muqaddimah as it represents the first stage of the emergence of this science, before its mixing with philosophy, and it almost expresses the opinion of the majority of those engaged in this science. Ibn Khaldun says: 'It is a science that contains arguing in defense of the creedal beliefs using rational proofs, and refuting the innovators who deviate in beliefs from the way of the Salaf or Ahl al-Sunnah.' And the definition given by Ibn Khaldun gives us, upon examination and reflection, that ilm al-kalam is a science that defends creedal beliefs. Its defensive weapons are reason and its tools. And it is always brandished in the face of misled innovators. If that is the case, then what is the name of the other (science) that is used by the opponents of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah from the Jahmiyyah, Khawarij, Batiniyyah, and the rest of the misled sects that deviate from the way of the Salaf? Indeed, the author of the book 'Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun' also asks: 'Does ilm al-kalam include defense of the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah only, or does it include all creeds related to the principles of religion, whether agreeing or opposing? And if...' (1) Refer to Muqaddimah Ibn Khaldun p. 448, al-Maktaba al-Tijariyya al-Kubra, Egypt. And al-Farabi said: 'Kalam is a craft by which a person is able to support the opinions and actions prescribed by the founder of the religion, and to refute whatever opposes them from the sayings' (Ihsa' al-'Ulum, pp. 71-72). (2) Imam al-Ghazali said: 'When the form of kalam arose and discussion increased, the mutakallimun became eager to attempt to defend the Sunnah by investigating the realities of things, and they delved into the investigation of substances and accidents and their rulings, but since that was not their goal, their speech did not reach the ultimate end' (al-Munqidh min al-Dalal, chapter on ilm al-kalam).
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Khaldun's definition of ilm al-kalam and then examines its implications. The author first explains why he chooses Ibn Khaldun's definition: it represents the early stage of kalam before it mixed with philosophy, and it reflects the majority view of practitioners. The definition itself states that kalam is a science that uses rational proofs to argue in defense of creedal beliefs (al-‘aqa’id al-imaniyya) and to refute innovators who deviate from the way of the Salaf or Ahl al-Sunnah. The author then draws three key features from this definition: 1) kalam defends creedal beliefs, 2) its weapons are reason and its tools, 3) it is always directed against misled innovators. After this analysis, the author raises an important question: if kalam is defined as defense of Ahl al-Sunnah, then what is the equivalent science used by opposing sects like the Jahmiyyah, Khawarij, and Batiniyyah? He then cites a question from the author of 'Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun' that asks whether kalam includes defense of only Ahl al-Sunnah or all creeds. The passage ends with footnotes providing additional definitions from al-Farabi and al-Ghazali, which support the idea that kalam is a tool for defending religious doctrines, though al-Ghazali notes that later practitioners delved into metaphysics beyond the original aim.

Key Terms
ابن خلدون
الحجاج
الأدلة العقلية
المبتدعة
مذهب السلف
أهل السنة
الجهمية
الخوارج
الباطنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think kalam is only about philosophical speculation or abstract theology.
Correction: Ibn Khaldun's definition shows that kalam is fundamentally an apologetic and defensive science focused on protecting creedal beliefs using rational arguments.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Khaldun's definition as presented in the passage, what are the main purposes of ilm al-kalam?
A) To establish philosophical truths and engage in metaphysical speculation.
B) To defend creedal beliefs using rational proofs and refute deviant innovators.
C) To study the history of religions and compare different creeds.
D) To provide a systematic theology independent of revelation.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Khaldun's definition frames kalam as a defensive science using rational proofs to protect Sunni creed, but it also raises a critical question about whether the discipline extends beyond one sect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face someone who challenges your beliefs, do you rely on rational proofs as described in this lesson, or do you fall back on empty slogans? What will you do this week to become a more effective defender of the creed?
?
Ibn Khaldun says kalam is 'always brandished in the face of misled innovators.' Is your knowledge of kalam sharp enough to refute the doubts of our time, or have you neglected this weapon? What is one specific doubt you will learn to answer?
?
The passage asks: if kalam is for Ahl al-Sunnah, what do the deviant sects use? Are you only a consumer of Islamic knowledge, or are you equipped to engage in reasoned argument against falsehood? What will you sacrifice to gain that skill?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
Ibn Khaldun's Definition of Ilm al-Kalam
Ibn Khaldun's definition of kalam and its threefold analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Khaldun's definition of ilm al-kalam and its three key aspects: defending creed, using rational proofs, and refuting heretical innovators.

Core Idea
Kalam is the rational defense of Islamic creed against heretical deviations.

Before diving into the detailed arguments of kalam, it is essential to have a clear understanding of what this science actually is. Ibn Khaldun, the renowned historian and philosopher, provides a definition that captures the essence of kalam in its early, pre-philosophical phase. This definition, which the author presents as representative of the majority view, highlights the defensive and rationally grounded nature of the discipline. As you read, notice how Ibn Khaldun emphasizes both the method (rational proofs) and the purpose (defense against innovators).

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read Ibn Khaldun's definition in Arabic and English. Note the key terms: 'argumentation', 'beliefs of faith', 'rational proofs', and 'refuting innovators'.
The definition is quoted verbatim; pay attention to its structure.
2
Examine the author's analysis
The author breaks the definition into three implications. List them: (1) kalam defends creed, (2) its weapons are reason, (3) it targets innovators.
These three points are the core of the lesson.
3
Reflect on the defensive nature
Consider why the author emphasizes defense. What does this tell you about the historical context of early kalam?
This connects to the misconception that kalam is pure speculation.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you grasp the definition's primary purpose.
The answer is directly in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أردنا أن نقدم بين يدي القارىء أحد هذه التعريفات، فإننا نختار التعريف الذي قدمه ابن خلدون في مقدمته باعتباره يمثل المرحلة الأولى من نشأة هذا العلم، قبل اختلاطه بالفلسفة، وهو مع ذلك يكاد يعبر عن رأي الأغلبية ممن يشتغلون بهذا العلم . 
يقول ابن خلدون : وهو علم يتضمن الحجاج عن العقائد الإيمانة بالأدلة العقلية، والرد على المبتدعة المنحرفين في الاعتقادات عن مذهب السلف، أو أهل السنة . 
والتعريف الذي قدمه ابن خلدون يعطينا عند فحصه وتأمله أن علم الكلام علم يدافع عن العقائد الإيمانية . 
وأسلحته الدفاعية هي العقل ومعداته . 
وهو دائماً يشهر في وجه المبتدعة الضالين .
And if we wish to present one of these definitions to the reader, we choose the definition given by Ibn Khaldun in his Muqaddimah, since it represents the first stage of the origin of this science, before it mixed with philosophy, and yet it almost expresses the opinion of the majority of those who engage in this science. Ibn Khaldun says: It is a science that includes argumentation about the beliefs of faith using rational proofs, and refuting innovators who deviate in their beliefs from the way of the Salaf or the People of the Sunnah. The definition given by Ibn Khaldun gives us, upon examination and contemplation, that ilm al-kalam is a science that defends the beliefs of faith. Its defensive weapons are reason and its instruments. And it is always wielded against the misguided innovators.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents and explains Ibn Khaldun's definition of ilm al-kalam. It begins by stating the author's choice of this definition as representative of the early stage of the science before it mixed with philosophy. Then it quotes Ibn Khaldun's definition verbatim: kalam is argumentation about creedal beliefs with rational proofs, and refutation of heretical innovators who deviate from the Salaf or Ahl al-Sunna. Next, the author analyzes the definition into three implications: (1) Kalam defends Islamic creed. (2) Its defensive tools are reason and its instruments (i.e., logic and rational argumentation). (3) It is always directed against misguided innovators. The definition highlights the apologetic nature of kalam in its early phase.

Key Terms
الحجاج
العقائد الإيمانية
الأدلة العقلية
المبتدعة
مذهب السلف
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ilm al-kalam is purely speculative philosophy detached from creed.
Correction: Ibn Khaldun's definition shows kalam is fundamentally defensive of Islamic beliefs and grounded in rational arguments aimed at refuting heretical deviations.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Khaldun's definition as presented, what is the primary purpose of ilm al-kalam?
A) To explore philosophical questions
B) To defend Islamic beliefs with rational proofs and refute heretics
C) To derive legal rulings
D) To study Aristotelian logic

Key Takeaway
Ibn Khaldun defines ilm al-kalam as the rational defense of Islamic creed against heretical innovations, using reason as its primary weapon.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Khaldun says kalam's weapons are reason and its instruments. In your own life, where have you used reason to defend your faith against doubts? Identify one doubt you've avoided confronting. Will you commit this week to seeking a rational Islamic response to that doubt from reliable sources?
?
The definition states kalam is 'always wielded against misguided innovators.' Have you ever encountered someone who holds a belief that deviates from the way of the Salaf? How did you react—did you ignore it, argue emotionally, or try to correct it with knowledge? What one step can you take to better equip yourself to gently address such deviations?
?
Reflect: is your iman simply inherited from your family and community, or have you actively defended it with reason? Ibn Khaldun's definition implies that a Muslim should be able to give rational proofs for their creed. Write down one Islamic belief you hold but cannot yet defend logically. What resource will you use to learn its rational proof before this week ends?

Is Ilm al-Kalam Exclusive to Ahl al-Sunna?
The author raises the question of whether kalam is exclusively for Ahl al-Sunna or includes other sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the terminological question of whether ilm al-kalam is exclusive to Ahl al-Sunna or encompasses all theological creeds.

Core Idea
Ilm al-kalam's scope is debated: is it Ahl al-Sunna's defensive weapon, or a universal theological method?

Sanusi presents a crucial question that arises from defining kalam as a defensive tool for Ahl al-Sunna. If that definition is accepted, what do we call the similar arguments used by opponent sects? The author of Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun poses this terminological dilemma, which we will explore in this passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own flow come through before interpreting.
Notice how the passage begins with a conditional statement.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage presents two options: either kalam is exclusive to Ahl al-Sunna, or it includes all creeds. Find where these are stated.
3
Consider the terminological gap
If kalam is exclusive, then what do we call the opponent's science? This highlights the need for a broader term or a separate classification.
The passage quotes Kashshaf to emphasize this point.
4
Reflect on the implications
This question suggests that the definition of kalam may be tied to its historical role in defending orthodoxy. Think about how this affects the study of other theological traditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان ذلك كذلك. فبماذا يسمى الآخر الذي يستعمله خصوم أهل السنة والجماعة من الجهمية والخوارج والباطنية، وبقية الفرق الضالة الخارجة عن مذهب السلف؟ .
إن صاحب كتاب (كشاف اصطلاحات الفنون) يتساءل أيضاً فيقول: «هل علم الكلام يشمل الدفاع عن عقيدة أهل السنة والجماعة فقط؟ أو يشمل كل العقائد المتعلقة بأصول الدين؟ سواء منها الموافق، أو المخالف؟ وإذا كان الجواب بالنفي، فبماذا يسمى العلم الآخر، العلم الذي يستعمله الخصوم في الرد والمقارعة ومحاولة الغلبة»؟
And if that is the case, then what is the name given to the other (science) used by the opponents of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, such as the Jahmiyyah, Khawarij, Batinis, and the rest of the deviant sects that have departed from the way of the Salaf? The author of Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun also asks: 'Does ilm al-kalam include only the defense of the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah? Or does it include all creeds related to the principles of religion, both those agreeing and disagreeing? And if the answer is negative, then what is the name of the other science, the science that the opponents use in refutation, confrontation, and attempts to gain victory?'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage raises a critical question about the scope of ilm al-kalam. It begins by noting that if kalam is defined as defending Ahl al-Sunna's creed with rational arguments, then what should we call the similar activity performed by opposing sects (Jahmiyya, Khawarij, Batinis, etc.)? The author then quotes from Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun, which asks whether kalam covers only Ahl al-Sunna's defense or all theological creeds. If it is exclusive, then the opponent's science would need a different name. This highlights a terminological problem: is kalam a specific science of Ahl al-Sunna, or a general method used by all theological factions? The passage sets up the need to investigate the origins and scope of kalam.

Key Terms
خصوم أهل السنة والجماعة
الجهمية
الخوارج
الباطنية
الفرق الضالة
كشاف اصطلاحات الفنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ilm al-kalam is a universal neutral science applicable to all sects equally.
Correction: Historically, kalam was primarily developed as a defensive tool for Ahl al-Sunna, and this passage asks whether it can be considered exclusive to them or if it includes all theologies.

Checkpoint
What issue does the author of Kashshaf Istilahat al-Funun raise?
A) Whether kalam is a rational science
B) Whether kalam is exclusive to Ahl al-Sunna or includes all theological creeds
C) Whether kalam has Greek origins
D) Whether kalam is forbidden

Key Takeaway
This passage highlights a fundamental terminological question about the scope of ilm al-kalam: is it exclusive to Ahl al-Sunna or does it encompass all theological discourse?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone who uses rational arguments to defend beliefs different from yours, do you automatically dismiss their theology as 'not real kalam'? How does that attitude affect your willingness to engage with their arguments?
?
Have you ever assumed that the way you define a religious term (like 'ilm al-kalam') is the only correct or valid definition? What would it take for you to genuinely consider that others might have a different, yet legitimate, understanding?
?
The author asks whether kalam should include both Sunni and non-Sunni creeds. How do you tend to categorize theological discourse that disagrees with your own tradition? Do you give it the same intellectual respect, or do you label it as something lesser? What does your answer reveal about your own biases?

The Quranic Roots of Ilm al-Kalam
The author examines the factors that led to the emergence of ilm al-Kalam, emphasizing the Quranic foundation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran served as the foundational source for the emergence of ilm al-Kalam, according to classical scholars.

Core Idea
The Quran is the fountainhead of kalam, not an import from Greek philosophy.

This lesson explores why scholars assert that ilm al-Kalam is rooted in the Quran itself. We will see how pre-Islamic Arabia lacked this science, yet the Quran provided decisive proofs that later became the foundation of kalam methodology. Authorities like al-Qushayri and al-Zarkashi argue that the Quran contains all rational proofs, albeit in a style suited to its original audience.

Guided Path
1
Understand the question about kalam's origins
The passage opens by asking how kalam emerged and what factors contributed. It notes kalam was absent in pre-Islamic Arabia.
2
Examine al-Qushayri's statement on Quranic verses
Al-Qushayri points out that verses on principles (usul) far outnumber legal verses, countering the claim that the Quran lacks kalam.
This is evidence of Quranic rational discourse.
3
Review al-Zarkashi's claim about the Quran's comprehensiveness
Al-Zarkashi asserts that the Quran contains every proof and definition, but in a concise Arabic style that requires deep reflection to extract kalam methods.
4
Synthesize Dr. Suleiman Dunya's affirmation
He confirms the Quran's fundamental role and rejects the idea that it hinders rational thought.
This concludes the passage's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل الإجابة على ذلك، نتساءل كيف نشأ علم الكلام في حياة المسلمين . . ؟ أعني ما هي العوامل التي ساعدت على إيجاده، ومازالت به حتى أصلته، ووضعت له المبادىء والقواعد الأساسية..؟ وإذا كان هذا العلم لم يعرف في البيئة العربية، قبل ظهور الإسلام، وقبل مبعث الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم أيكون القرآن الكريم وما فيه من أدلة قاطعة وبراهين ساطعة، هو أحد العوامل الأساسية في إنشاء علم الكلام؟
إن ابن عساكر في كتبه تبيين كذب المفتري يروي عن الإمام القشيري قوله : «والعجب ممن يقول : ليس في القرآن علم الكلام.
والآيات التي هي في الأحكام الشرعية نجدها محصورة، والآيات المنبهة على علم الأصول نجدها توفي على ذلك، وتربى بكثير من الزيادة».
ويقول صاحب البرهان : وما من برهان ودلالة وتقسيم وتحديد شيء من كليات المعلومات العقلية والسمعية إلا كتاب الله تعالى قد نطق به. لكن أورده تعالى على عادة العرب، دون دقائق طرق أحكام المتكلمين». ثم يقول : واعلم أنه قد يظهر منه بدقيق الفكر استنباط البراهين العقلية، على طرق المتلكمين».
والدكتور سليمان دنيا يقرر أن الدور الأساسي في نشأة علم الكلام كان للقرآن وينكر بقوة دعوى البعض أن القرآن يعوق النظر العقلي.
Before answering that, we ask: How did ilm al-kalam arise in the life of Muslims? I mean, what are the factors that helped bring it about, and continued until it was established, and the principles and basic rules were laid down? And if this science was not known in the Arab environment before the advent of Islam and before the mission of the Messenger (peace be upon him), could it be that the Noble Quran, with its decisive proofs and brilliant evidences, is one of the fundamental factors in the emergence of ilm al-kalam? Ibn Asakir in his book Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari narrates from Imam al-Qushayri that he said: 'It is astonishing that someone says that there is no kalam in the Quran. The verses on legal rulings are limited, while the verses that point to the principles (usul) are abundant and far exceed them in number.' The author of al-Burhan says: 'There is no proof, indication, division, or definition of any of the universal categories of rational and revealed knowledge except that the Book of God has expressed it. But God has presented it according to Arab custom, without the fine details of the methods of the mutakallimun.' Then he says: 'Know that through precise thought, the extraction of rational proofs in the manner of the mutakallimun can appear from it.' Dr. Suleiman Dunya affirms that the fundamental role in the emergence of ilm al-kalam was for the Quran, and he strongly denies the claim of some that the Quran impedes rational speculation.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage investigates the origins of ilm al-kalam in Islamic history. It begins by posing the question: how did kalam emerge, and what factors contributed to its development? It notes that kalam was unknown in pre-Islamic Arabia, suggesting that the Quran itself, with its rational arguments, was a key factor. The author then provides evidence from authorities: Imam al-Qushayri (via Ibn Asakir) expresses astonishment at those who deny the presence of kalam in the Quran, pointing out that Quranic verses on principles (usul) are far more numerous than legal verses. Then the author of al-Burhan (al-Zarkashi) argues that the Quran contains every type of proof, division, and definition of rational and revealed knowledge, but in a style suitable for Arabs, not in the technical language of the mutakallimun. However, through deep reflection, one can derive rational proofs in the manner of kalam. Finally, Dr. Suleiman Dunya reinforces that the Quran was the primary factor in kalam's emergence, rejecting the claim that the Quran hinders rational inquiry. Thus, the passage establishes a strong Quranic foundation for kalam, countering accusations that it is an alien innovation.

القرآن الكريم
أدلة قاطعة
براهين ساطعة
الإمام القشيري
ابن عساكر
تبيين كذب المفتري
البرهان
المتكلمين
سليمان دنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That ilm al-Kalam is purely a Greek import and has no roots in the Quran.
Correction: This passage shows that the Quran itself contains rational proofs and principles that formed the foundation of kalam, as affirmed by classical scholars.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do Ibn Asakir and al-Qushayri point out about the Quran?
A) It contains no rational arguments
B) It has more verses on principles (usul) than on legal rulings
C) It forbids speculation
D) It uses Greek philosophical terms

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the primary source of ilm al-Kalam, providing decisive proofs and principles that scholars later systematized.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you approach the Quran expecting to find rational arguments, or do you limit it to commands and stories? How will you change your reading starting today?
?
You have heard that the Quran is the source of kalam. But have you ever extracted a rational proof from the Quran for a belief you hold? Commit to doing that this week for one article of faith.
?
If the Quran contains the seeds of theological reasoning, why do you sometimes rely on weak arguments or blind following? What would it cost you to become someone who can reason from the Quran itself?

What Is Kalam?

The Objection to Ilm al-Kalam: Why Some Said It Was Unnecessary
Presents the objection that ilm al-kalam was unnecessary because Quran and Sunnah suffice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objections raised against ilm al-kalam, including the claim that Quran and Sunnah suffice and the argument from prophetic silence.

Core Idea
The objection to kalam rests on the assumption that Quran and Sunnah are sufficient and that innovation is blameworthy.

This lesson presents the objections of those who argued that ilm al-kalam was unnecessary. They reasoned that the Quran and Sunnah already establish all needed doctrines, and that if kalam were beneficial, the Prophet and his Companions would have engaged in it. Understanding these objections is crucial before examining the responses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the objector's argument come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author is presenting an objection, not his own view.
2
Identify the main claim
The objectors claim that Quran and Sunnah suffice for doctrine, so there is no need for a separate science of kalam. Find where this is stated.
This is the foundation of the objection.
3
Analyse the first argument
The first argument is from prophetic silence: if kalam were guidance, the Prophet and his Companions would have spoken about it. Since they did not, speaking about kalam is innovation (bid'a).
Note the underlying assumption that the Prophet left nothing unexplained.
4
Analyse the second argument (the dilemma)
The second argument presents a dilemma: either the early Muslims (Salaf) knew kalam and remained silent, implying we should too, or they did not know it, implying it is unnecessary.
The dilemma forces a conclusion that kalam is either superfluous or blameworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هل كان المسلمون في حاجة إليه . . ؟ ونتساءل هل كان المسلمون بحاجة إلى علم الكلام حين قام؟ يرى بعض العلماء أن العقائد ثابتة في القرآن وأوضحتها السنة النبوية فلا حاجة إذن إلى علم الكلام. هذا على اعتبار أن علم الكلام هو علم يقتدر معه على إثبات العقائد الدينية على الغير بإيراد الحجج ودفع الشبه .. كما يقول (التفتازاني) في شرحه للعقائد العضدية (١) . ويقولون أيضاً : لو كان علم الكلام هدى ورشاداً لتكلم فيه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وخلفاؤه وأصحابه ، ولأن النبي لم لما لم يمت حتى تكلم في كل ما يحتاج إليه من الله أمور الدين، وبينه بياناً ،شافياً، ولم يترك بعده لأحد مقالاً فيما للمسلمين إليه حاجة من أمور دينهم، وما يقربهم إلى الله عز وجل، ويباعدهم عن سخطه، فلما لم يرووا عنه الكلام في شيء مما ذكرناه علمنا أن الكلام فيه بدعة، والبحث عنه ضلالة لأنه لو كان خيراً لما فات النبي راً لما فات النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولتكلموا فيه . وقالوا أيضاً ولأنه ليس يخلو ذلك من وجهين : إما أن يكونوا علموه فسكتوا : أو لم يعلموه بل جهلوه، فإن كانوا علموه ولم يتكلموا فيه وسعنا أيضاً نحن السكوت عنه، كما وسعهم السكوت عنه ووسعنا ترك الخوض فيه، كما
Were the Muslims in need of it? ... And we ask: Were the Muslims in need of ilm al-kalam when it arose? Some scholars hold that the creeds are established in the Qur'an and clarified by the Prophetic Sunnah, so there is no need for ilm al-kalam. This is on the consideration that ilm al-kalam is a science by which one is able to establish religious doctrines against others by presenting proofs and repelling doubts, as al-Taftazani says in his commentary on al-'Aqa'id al-'Adudiyya. And they also say: If ilm al-kalam were guidance and rectitude, the Prophet (peace be upon him), his caliphs, and his companions would have spoken about it. And because the Prophet did not die until he had spoken about everything needed from Allah regarding matters of religion, and explained it fully, and left no room for anyone after him to speak about what the Muslims need of their religious affairs, and what brings them closer to Allah and distances them from His anger. Since they did not report from him any speech about anything we have mentioned, we know that speaking about it is innovation (bid'a), and researching it is misguidance, because if it were good, the Prophet would not have missed it, and they would have spoken about it. And they also said: And because that is not free from two aspects: either they knew it and remained silent, or they did not know it but were ignorant of it. If they knew it and did not speak about it, then it is also permissible for us to remain silent about it, just as it was permissible for them to remain silent about it, and it is permissible for us to refrain from delving into it, just as
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the objection of those who argue that ilm al-kalam was unnecessary and even blameworthy. The author begins by raising the question: Were the Muslims in need of ilm al-kalam when it arose? He then reports the view of some scholars that the doctrines are already fixed in the Qur'an and clarified by the Sunnah, so there is no need for a separate science of kalam. The definition used here, attributed to al-Taftazani, is that kalam is a science enabling one to establish religious doctrines against others by presenting proofs and repelling doubts. The objectors then provide two main arguments. First, if kalam were guidance, the Prophet, his caliphs, and companions would have spoken about it. Since the Prophet explained all necessary matters of religion and did not leave anything out, and since no speech about kalam is reported from them, it must be an innovation (bid'a) and researching it is misguidance. Second, they present a dilemma: either the early Muslims (the Salaf) knew kalam and remained silent about it, or they did not know it. If they knew it and remained silent, then we too should remain silent. If they did not know it, then it is not needed. The passage ends abruptly at 'just as' (kama), indicating that the argument continues, likely to be concluded or answered later. The author is presenting these objections as part of a larger discussion, likely to refute them subsequently.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
إثبات العقائد
بدعة
هدى ورشاد
السنة النبوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This objection is the author's own view.
Correction: The author is presenting the objection of others in order to refute it later in the text.

Checkpoint
What are the two possibilities presented in the dilemma against ilm al-kalam?
A) Either the Salaf knew kalam and taught it, or they did not know it.
B) Either the Salaf knew kalam and remained silent, or they did not know it.
C) Either the Salaf wrote books on kalam, or they rejected it.
D) Either the Prophet engaged in kalam, or his companions did.

Key Takeaway
The main objection to ilm al-kalam is that if it were beneficial, the Prophet and early Muslims would have practiced it, and since they did not, it is an innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not engage in ilm al-kalam, how do you justify spending your time studying it? Is your study driven by a genuine need to defend the truth, or by intellectual curiosity that may not please Allah?
?
The objectors argue that the Quran and Sunnah are sufficient. When you encounter a complex theological question, do you first turn to revelation or to human reasoning? Where does your trust truly lie?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment and He asks you about the time you spent learning kalam. What will you say? Will it be a proof for you or against you? How can you ensure that your study remains a means of drawing closer to Him?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
Objections to Ilm al-Kalam: The Case Against
The author enumerates opponents' objections to ilm al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main objections raised against the need for ilm al-kalam, including the argument from prophetic silence and the dilemma of early Muslim practice.

Core Idea
Opponents argue that if ilm al-kalam were needed, the Prophet would have practiced it.

Before answering the objections, the author faithfully presents them. This passage records why some scholars consider ilm al-kalam an unnecessary innovation. You will see two main arguments: one based on the Prophet's silence, and a dilemma about early Muslims. Pay attention to the logic — these are not the author's own views but the views he will refute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Let the opponents' case be heard.
The author is presenting the opponents' arguments, not his own.
2
Identify the first argument
The opponents argue that if kalam were guidance, the Prophet and his companions would have spoken about it. Since they did not, it must be an innovation.
This is an argument from silence.
3
Identify the second argument
The opponents present a dilemma: either early Muslims knew kalam and remained silent, or they were ignorant of it. In either case, later Muslims can also remain silent or be ignorant.
The dilemma is meant to show that kalam cannot be part of religion.
4
Note the conclusion
The opponents conclude that speaking about kalam is an innovation (bid‘a) and delving into it is misguidance (dalāla).
This sets up the refutation that will follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هل كان المسلمون في حاجة إليه . . ؟ ونتساءل هل كان المسلمون بحاجة إلى علم الكلام حين قام؟ يرى بعض العلماء أن العقائد ثابتة في القرآن وأوضحتها السنة النبوية فلا حاجة إذن إلى علم الكلام. هذا على اعتبار أن علم الكلام هو علم يقتدر معه على إثبات العقائد الدينية على الغير بإيراد الحجج ودفع الشبه .. كما يقول (التفتازاني) في شرحه للعقائد العضدية. ويقولون أيضاً : لو كان علم الكلام هدى ورشاداً لتكلم فيه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وخلفاؤه وأصحابه ، ولأن النبي لم يمت حتى تكلم في كل ما يحتاج إليه من أمور الدين، وبينه بياناً شافياً، ولم يترك بعده لأحد مقالاً فيما للمسلمين إليه حاجة من أمور دينهم، وما يقربهم إلى الله عز وجل، ويباعدهم عن سخطه، فلما لم يرووا عنه الكلام في شيء مما ذكرناه علمنا أن الكلام فيه بدعة، والبحث عنه ضلالة لأنه لو كان خيراً لما فات النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولتكلموا فيه . وقالوا أيضاً ولأنه ليس يخلو ذلك من وجهين : إما أن يكونوا علموه فسكتوا : أو لم يعلموه بل جهلوه، فإن كانوا علموه ولم يتكلموا فيه وسعنا أيضاً نحن السكوت عنه، كما وسعهم السكوت عنه ووسعنا ترك الخوض فيه، كما وسعهم ترك الخوض فيه، ولأنه لو كان من الدين ما وسعهم السكوت عنه، وإن كانوا لم يعلموه وسعنا جهله، كما وسع أولئك جهله، لأنه لو كان من الدين لم يجهلوه، فعلى كلا الوجهين الكلام فيه بدعة، والخوض فيه ضلالة. ولسنا في حاجة إليه كما كان المسلمون الأول في غير حاجة إليه .
Were the Muslims in need of it? And we ask: Were the Muslims in need of the science of kalam when it arose? Some scholars hold that creeds are established in the Quran and clarified by the Sunnah, so there is no need for the science of kalam. This is based on the view that the science of kalam is a science by which one is able to establish religious creeds to others by presenting proofs and repelling doubts, as al-Taftazani says in his commentary on al-Aqa'id al-‘Adudiyya. And they also say: If the science of kalam had been guidance and right guidance, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would have spoken about it, as would his caliphs and companions. And because the Prophet did not die until he had spoken about everything needed from matters of religion, and explained it with a sufficient explanation, and left no room after him for anyone to speak about what Muslims need from their religious affairs, and what brings them near to Allah Almighty and distances them from His wrath. Since they did not report from him any speech about anything we have mentioned, we know that speaking about it is an innovation and researching it is misguidance, because if it were good, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would not have missed it and they would have spoken about it. And they also said: And because that case is not free from two aspects: either they knew it and remained silent, or they did not know it but were ignorant of it. If they knew it and did not speak about it, then it is also permissible for us to remain silent about it, just as it was permissible for them to remain silent about it, and it is permissible for us to refrain from delving into it, just as it was permissible for them to refrain from delving into it. And because if it were part of religion, it would not have been permissible for them to remain silent about it. And if they did not know it, then ignorance of it is permissible for us, just as ignorance of it was permissible for those (early Muslims), because if it were part of religion, they would not have been ignorant of it. Thus, in both cases, speaking about it is an innovation and delving into it is misguidance. And we have no need for it, just as the early Muslims had no need for it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the objections of those who argue that ilm al-kalam is unnecessary and even blameworthy. The objectors begin by asking whether early Muslims needed this science when it arose. They note that some scholars hold that Islamic creeds are fully established in the Quran and clarified by the Sunnah, so there is no need for a separate science of kalam. They define kalam (as per al-Taftazani) as a discipline that enables one to prove religious doctrines to others by presenting arguments and repelling doubts. The objectors then advance two main arguments. First, if kalam were truly guidance and right guidance, the Prophet (s) and his companions would have engaged in it. But the Prophet explained everything needed for religion and left no need for additional discourse. Since no such discourse is reported from him, engaging in kalam must be an innovation (bid‘a) and misguidance. Second, they present a dilemma: either the early Muslims knew kalam and remained silent about it, or they were ignorant of it. If they knew it and remained silent, then we may also remain silent. If they were ignorant of it, then ignorance is permissible for us as well, because if it were part of religion they would not have been ignorant. In either case, speaking about kalam is an innovation and delving into it is misguidance. They conclude that we have no need for it, just as early Muslims had no need. The passage faithfully records the opponents' arguments, which the author will later refute.

Key Terms
علم الكلام (ilm al-kalam)
بدعة (bid‘a)
ضلالة (dalāla)
الحجج (ḥujaj)
الشبه (shubah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The readers might think that the author endorses these objections against ilm al-kalam.
Correction: The author is presenting the opponents' arguments faithfully in order to refute them later. He does not hold these views himself.

Checkpoint
What dilemma do the opponents use to argue that ilm al-kalam is unnecessary?
A) Either the early Muslims knew kalam and taught it, or they were ignorant and learned it later.
B) Either the early Muslims knew kalam and remained silent, or they were ignorant of it; in both cases, later Muslims may also remain silent or be ignorant.
C) Either the early Muslims wrote books on kalam, or they did not; since they did not, it is forbidden.
D) Either the Prophet spoke about kalam, or he did not; since he did not, it is permissible to speak.

Key Takeaway
Opponents of ilm al-kalam argue that its absence from prophetic practice and the early Muslim community proves it is an unnecessary innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at your own life: are there areas of Islamic knowledge you avoid because they feel unfamiliar or difficult? When you encounter a practice or study like ilm al-kalam that wasn't explicitly done by the Prophet, do you sincerely examine its benefit or do you use the 'silence argument' as an excuse to avoid engaging with hard questions? Ask yourself: Is your reluctance driven by sincere caution or spiritual laziness? This lesson forces you to confront that.
?
The opponents' argument relies on the assumption that if something is not done by the early Muslims, it must be innovation. But what about your own soul? Are there truths you ignore simply because they weren't part of your upbringing? Today, choose one area of your faith that you've neglected—perhaps theology or defending your creed—and commit to learning about it with an open heart, seeking Allah's guidance rather than using the comfort of tradition as an excuse.

The Argument that Kalam is a Forbidden Innovation
A logical argument to show kalam is a forbidden innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument used to claim that ilm al-kalam is a forbidden innovation based on the practice of the early Muslims.

Core Idea
The early Muslims' silence proves kalam is not from religion, so it is bid'ah.

This passage presents a powerful argument against the permissibility of kalam based on the practice of the early Muslims. The author uses a two-part logical reasoning to show that kalam cannot be part of the religion, and therefore engaging in it is blameworthy. Let's examine the argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the logical structure: the author uses conditionals.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the two conditional statements
The author presents two 'if...then' arguments. Find them and notice their structure. Each leads to the same conclusion.
One conditional uses 'if it were from religion...' and the other uses 'if they were ignorant of it...'.
3
Understand how each leads to the conclusion
Work through each conditional: The first shows that the early Muslims' silence implies kalam is not obligatory. The second shows that their ignorance makes it permissible for us to be ignorant. Both lead to the conclusion that kalam is bid'ah.
The author says 'on both counts' to sum up.
4
Reflect on the final sentence
The passage ends with 'We have no need of it, just as the early Muslims had no need.' Consider what this implies about the value of kalam.
This reinforces the conclusion that kalam is not a praiseworthy science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسعهم ترك الخوض فيه، ولأنه لو كان من الدين ما وسعهم السكوت عنه، وإن كانوا لم يعلموه وسعنا جهله، كما وسع أولئك جهله، لأنه لو كان من الدين لم يجهلوه، فعلى كلا الوجهين الكلام فيه بدعة، والخوض فيه ضلالة . ولسنا في حاجة إليه كما كان المسلمون الأول في غير حاجة إليه .
It was permissible for them to refrain from engaging in it, and because if it were from religion, it would not have been permissible for them to remain silent about it. And if they did not know it, then it is permissible for us to be ignorant of it, just as it was permissible for those to be ignorant of it, because if it were from religion, they would not have been ignorant of it. So on both counts, engaging in it is an innovation (bidʿah) and delving into it is misguidance (ḍalālah). And we have no need of it, just as the early Muslims had no need of it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents a logical argument to demonstrate that ilm al-kalam is a forbidden innovation. The author begins by stating a premise: the early Muslims were permitted to refrain from engaging in kalam. The reasoning is that if kalam were truly part of the religion, they would not have been permitted to remain silent about it, because religious obligations must be conveyed. Furthermore, if the early Muslims were ignorant of kalam, then it is permissible for later generations to be ignorant of it as well, because if it were an essential part of religion, the early Muslims would not have been ignorant of it. Thus, the author concludes that from both perspectives—whether the early Muslims knew it or not—kalam is a bidʿah (innovation) and delving into it is ḍalālah (misguidance). The final sentence reinforces that we have no need for kalam, just as the early Muslims had no need for it, implying that it is not a necessary or praiseworthy science.

Key Terms
بدعة
ضلالة
الخوض
السكوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if the early Muslims did not practice kalam, it is merely permissible and not blameworthy.
Correction: The author argues it is actually blameworthy and forbidden, as it is an innovation and misguidance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it permissible for us to be ignorant of kalam?
A) Because kalam is a difficult science that only a few can master.
B) Because the early Muslims were ignorant of it, and if it were from religion they would not have been ignorant.
C) Because the Prophet ﷺ forbade speaking about theological matters.
D) Because kalam leads to innovation and misguidance regardless of context.

Key Takeaway
The early Muslims' lack of engagement with kalam proves it is not part of religion and thus a blameworthy innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says we have no need of kalam just as the early Muslims had no need. Think about your own study of Islamic theology: are there areas you spend time on that the early Muslims never engaged in? How does this make you feel about the spiritual priority of such study? What is one step you can take this week to prioritize what they prioritized?
?
If the early Muslims' silence proves that delving into theological speculation is misguidance, then what about your own conversations and debates on social media or in study circles? Are you spending time on matters they were silent about? How can you redirect that time to something that was part of their practice?
?
This lesson challenges the very foundation of theological reasoning. When you are faced with a question about faith that the early Muslims did not discuss, do you feel compelled to find an answer through rational argument, or are you content to remain silent like they did? What is holding you back from surrendering to their way?

The Necessity of Kalam Against Modern Heresies
Author argues for continued need of kalam and lists modern heresies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that kalam is needed today, and what modern anti-Islamic ideologies (Jahmiyya, nominalism, empiricism, rationalism) are described as threats.

Core Idea
Kalam is not just history—it is the weapon against modern ideologies that deny revelation.

The author poses a critical question: do Muslims need kalam today? He anticipates some may say no, but then asks how we can counter modern forms of heresy that go beyond the classical ones. This passage identifies several contemporary intellectual movements that attack the Quran and the concept of God, arguing that kalam is essential for defending the faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with attention to the rhetorical questions
Notice how the author uses questions to build his argument for necessity.
The questions are not answered directly but imply the need for kalam.
2
Identify the three modern schools
The passage mentions nominalism, empiricism, and rationalism. Understand their core claims.
These are not classical kalam terms but modern philosophical movements.
3
Reflect on the role of kalam
Why does kalam provide the tools to refute these ideologies?
Consider that kalam deals with rational arguments for belief in God and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصل بذلك إلى السؤال الثالث: هل المسلمون الآن بحاجة إلى الكلام؟ وهل يعطينا درس نشأته عبرة استمراره ..؟ وإذا كان الجواب بالنفي، وهو أن المسلمين الآن ليسوا في حاجة إليه، فكيف نرد طغيان جهمية القرن العشرين ..؟ لقد كانت الجهمية الأولى تقول : إن القرآن كلام الله مخلوق؟ أما الجهمية الحديثة المتثلة في الاستشراق وأتباعه، والتبشير وأذنابه، فإنها تقول ببشرية القرآن ـ أي أن القرآن مصنوع ومؤلف . قام بتأليفه محمد وهو مرآة مكة لأفق خاص من الحياة، هو أفق الحياة في شبه الجزيرة العربية وفي خاص (۱). بوجه كيف نحاجج المذاهب الحديثة الهدامة؟ وما وسيلتنا في الرد على المذهب الاسمي» الذي يقرر أتباعه - قاتلهم الله - أن لفظ الله لا يوجد لـه وكيف نحاجج أصحاب المذهب التجريبي» والذي يعبر عن مسمى أصوله ، لود) فيج (باخ) فيلسوف ألماني بقوله : أحد الله كان فكرتي الأولى والعقل كان فكرتي الثانية . والإنسان بمحيطه الواقعي هو فكرتي الثالثة والأخيرة» (٢) . كيف نحول بين مجتمعنا وبين الاستماع إلى هذه المذاهب التي تتسرب إليه عن طريق التلفاز تارة، والمذياع تارة أخرى. إن أتباع المذهب العقلي يسمون هذا العصر، عصر التنوير أو عصر الإنسان ويفسر (وولف) الألماني التنوير بقوله : «إقصاء الدين عن مجال التوجيه، وإحلال العقل محله». (۱) الفكر الإسلامي وصلته بالاستعمار الغربي : الدكتور محمد (۲) المصدر السابق . ٤٢
And we thus arrive at the third question: Are Muslims now in need of kalam? And does the lesson of its origin give us a lesson for its continuation...? If the answer is negative, that Muslims now are not in need of it, then how do we repel the tyranny of the Jahmiyya of the twentieth century? The first Jahmiyya used to say: The Quran is the created speech of Allah. As for the modern Jahmiyya, represented by Orientalism and its followers, and missionary activity and its tails, they say that the Quran is human — i.e. that the Quran is fabricated and authored. Muhammad authored it, and it is a mirror of Mecca for a particular horizon of life, the horizon of life in the Arabian Peninsula and in [particular] aspect. How do we argue against the destructive modern schools? And what is our means in refuting the 'nominalist' school, whose followers — may Allah curse them — assert that the word 'Allah' has no referent? And how do we argue against the proponents of the 'empiricist' school, which expresses its principles, according to [Ludwig] Feuerbach, a German philosopher, in his saying: 'God was my first idea, reason was my second idea, and man in his real environment is my third and last idea'? How do we prevent our society from listening to these schools which seep into it through television at times, and radio at other times? Indeed, the followers of the 'rationalist' school call this age the Age of Enlightenment or the Age of Man, and the German [Christian] Wolff interprets enlightenment as: 'The exclusion of religion from the field of guidance, and the substitution of reason in its place.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage addresses the continued relevance of kalam in the modern era. The author poses the third question: whether Muslims need kalam today, and whether studying its origins provides guidance for its continuation. He anticipates a negative answer (that Muslims do not need it) and responds by asking how then to counter the tyranny of the 'Jahmiyya of the twentieth century'. He explains that the original Jahmiyya claimed the Quran was created, but the modern Jahmiyya (Orientalism and missionaries) goes further, asserting that the Quran is purely human — authored by Muhammad and reflecting only the specific cultural horizon of 7th-century Arabia. The author then asks rhetorical questions about how to refute modern destructive schools: the 'nominalist' school (which denies that the word 'Allah' has a real referent) and the 'empiricist' school (exemplified by Feuerbach, who posits God, reason, and man as successive stages). He also mentions the 'rationalist' school which declares this the Age of Enlightenment, defined by Wolff as replacing religion with reason. The passage thus argues that kalam is necessary to defend Islam against these modern ideologies. Footnotes cite sources from contemporary writers.

Key Terms
جهمية القرن العشرين
بشرية القرآن
الاستشراق
التبشير
المذهب الاسمي
المذهب التجريبي
المذهب العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kalam is only concerned with theological debates from the early Islamic period.
Correction: This passage demonstrates kalam's relevance to modern ideologies such as Orientalism, secularism, and rationalism.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the modern Jahmiyya (Orientalists and missionaries) claim about the Quran?
A) It is the created speech of Allah
B) It is human, authored by Muhammad
C) It is the uncreated word of Allah
D) It is a combination of divine and human elements

Key Takeaway
The author argues that kalam is necessary today to counter modern ideologies that deny the divine origin of the Quran and the reality of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were confronted by someone who claims the Quran is simply Muhammad's own writing, would you be able to refute them using the tools of kalam? What is at stake if you cannot?
?
When you hear modern ideologies that elevate reason above revelation, such as the claim that enlightenment means excluding religion from guidance, does your heart tremble? Are you armed with arguments to defend the supremacy of divine guidance?
?
The author says the modern Jahmiyya 'seep into our society through television and radio.' Have you ever felt your own faith subtly eroded by such media? What steps will you take today to fortify your conviction against these infiltrations?

Linguistic Origin of Jadl from a Hadith
The author explains the linguistic origin of jadl using a Prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic root of the term 'jadl' as illustrated by a Prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
'Jadl' literally means being thrown down or entangled.

This lesson traces the term 'jadl' back to its literal meaning through a hadith of the Prophet. Before we study jadl as a technical term in kalam, we need to see its earthy origins. The hadith shows that even Adam was once 'munjadil' – lying on the ground.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic hadith and its translation. Note the word 'munjadil' and its connection to 'jadl'.
2
Identify the root meaning
Understand that 'jadl' in Arabic means to twist or throw down. The hadith illustrates this physical sense.
3
Connect to technical usage
Consider how this physical sense of twisting led to the technical meaning of debate as each debater tries to twist the other's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحديث عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : «أنا خاتم النبيين في أم الكتاب وإن آدم لمنجدل في طينته» أي ملقى على الجدالة الأرض.
And in the hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I am the seal of the prophets in the Mother of the Book, and Adam was still entwined in his clay' – i.e., thrown upon the ground [al-jadāla].
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage begins with a hadith to illustrate the linguistic origin of the term 'jadl' (جدل). The Prophet says he was the seal of prophets in the divine decree (Umm al-Kitab) while Adam was still 'munjadil' in his clay, meaning lying on the earth. The word 'munjadil' comes from the root j-d-l, which in its basic sense means to be twisted or thrown down. This gives the first clue to the technical meaning of jadl as debate: each debater tries to twist the other's argument.

Key Terms
جدل (jadl)
منجدل (munjadil)
جدالة (jadāla)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'jadl' initially meant arguing or debating.
Correction: It originally meant physical twisting or being thrown down, as shown in the hadith.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith about Adam being 'munjadil' indicate about the linguistic meaning of jadl?
A) It means to argue vehemently
B) It means to be thrown or entangled
C) It means to be victorious
D) It means to be patient

Key Takeaway
The linguistic root of 'jadl' is physical entanglement or being thrown down, as shown in the hadith of Adam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in debate (jadl), do you seek to throw your opponent down or to build understanding? The word jadl itself originates from being tossed onto the ground. Think of your last argument: was it about winning or about truth? What will you change in how you argue this week?
?
The Prophet’s decree as the final prophet was written while Adam was still 'munjadil' on the ground. Does this humbling truth affect your confidence in arguments? Do you enter debates aware that your opinion may be wrong? How can you keep that humility before your next disagreement?
?
If words can 'throw down' like physical entanglement, how carefully do you choose them in disagreements? What would it look like for you to use speech to lift up rather than to cast down in your next difficult conversation?

What Is Kalam?
beginner

Technical Definition of Jadl
The author gives the technical definition of jadl and quotes two earlier scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the technical definition of jadl (dialectical debate) as defined by the author and two classical scholars, distinguishing it from mere discussion.

Core Idea
Jadl is confrontational debate aimed at forcing an opponent, not open-ended discussion.

This lesson introduces the technical meaning of jadl, a core concept in Islamic dialectics. The author presents his own definition and then supports it with definitions from al-Jurjani and Abu al-Baqa, showing a consistent scholarly understanding. By studying these definitions, you will see how jadl is distinguished from other forms of debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the key terms: المفاوضة, المنازعة, المغالبة, إلزام الخصم.
These terms capture the confrontational nature of jadl.
2
Understand the author's definition
The author defines jadl as discussion in a disputatious and competitive manner to force the opponent. Reflect on each component.
The aim is ilzām al-khaṣm (forcing the opponent).
3
Examine al-Jurjani's definition
Al-Jurjani defines it as a method for manifesting and establishing doctrines. Notice it's about methodology, not just argument.
4
Examine Abu al-Baqa's definition
Abu al-Baqa emphasizes repelling corruption of one's statement by proof or doubt, and that it only occurs through disputation with others.
This highlights the defensive aspect.
5
Synthesize the three definitions
Combine the definitions: jadl is a structured, confrontational exchange aimed at either forcing an opponent or defending one's position through evidence.

الجدل اصطلاحاً : حقيقة الجدل : هو المفاوضة على سبيل المنازعة والمغالبة لإلزام الخصم . قال الجرجاني : الجدل عبارة عن مراد يتعلق بإظهار المذاهب وتقريرها وقال أبو البقاء في كتاب (الكليات) : «الجدل، هو عبارة عن دفع المرء فساد قوله بحجة أو شبهة وهو لا يكون إلا بمنازعة غيره
Jadl in technical terminology: The reality of jadl is: discussion in the manner of disputation and contention to force the opponent. Al-Jurjani said: 'Jadl is a term for a method attached to manifesting and establishing doctrines.' And Abu al-Baqa' said in his book al-Kulliyyat: 'Jadl is the expression for a person repelling the corruption of his statement by proof or doubt, and it only occurs through disputing with others.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage gives the technical definition of jadl. The author first defines it as discussion (mufāwaḍa) in a confrontational and competitive manner (munāza'a and mughālaba) with the aim of forcing the opponent (ilzām al-khaṣm). Then he quotes al-Jurjānī, who defines it as a method for displaying and confirming doctrines, and Abu al-Baqā', who defines it as defending one's statement against corruption by evidence or doubt, which only occurs through disputation.

Misconception: Jadl is merely any debate or discussion.
Correction: Jadl specifically involves disputation and the aim of forcing the opponent, not just open-ended discussion.

A) To display one's knowledge
B) To resolve a dispute amicably

Jadl is a confrontational, evidence-based debate aimed at forcing or defending against an opponent, as defined by classical scholars.
